6 min
Categorical and Disjunctive Propositions: Resemblance and Distinction
Explains resemblance between categorical and disjunctive propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a categorical proposition that resembles a disjunctive from a pure disjunctive based on the position of the subject and particle.

Core Idea
A categorical with two predicates can look like a disjunctive, but the subject's position betrays its true form.

This passage explains that categorical and disjunctive propositions can resemble each other, which is important for correct logical analysis. The key is the placement of the subject relative to the disjunctive particle: if the subject comes before the particle, it is a categorical resembling a disjunctive; if the particle comes first, it is a disjunctive resembling a categorical. Pure forms exist as well.

Guided Path
1
Identify whether there is a single subject
Check if the proposition has one subject that two predicates are attributed to. For example, in 'The number is either even or odd', the subject is 'the number'.
If there is no single subject, it is likely a pure disjunctive.
2
Locate the disjunctive particle (e.g., 'إما...أو')
Find the particle that sets up the alternatives. In example, it is 'إما...أو' (either...or).
3
Determine the position of the subject relative to the first particle
If the subject precedes the first particle (e.g., 'العدد إما زوج أو فرد'), it is a categorical resembling a disjunctive. If the particle comes first (e.g., 'إما أن يكون العدد زوجا أو فردا'), it is a disjunctive resembling a categorical.
This is the key differentia.
4
Classify as pure or resembling
If the proposition fits the pattern of having a subject before the particle with two predicates, it is categorical resembling disjunctive. If it has the particle first and no explicit subject, it is disjunctive resembling categorical. Otherwise, it is pure categorical or pure disjunctive.
The passage says pure forms are apparent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي النَّنَاقُضِ [ كيفيَّةُ التَّناقض في الموجهات المركبة] ٦٦٥ وأمَّا النَّقيضُ لِلْمُرَكَّب ) فهو (المنْهُوْمُ الْمُرَدَّدُ بَيْنَ نَقِيضَيِ الجُزْأَيْنِ)، الدسوقي وتحصل من هذا : أنَّ الضَّرورة بحسبِ الذَّاتِ يُقابلها الإمكانُ العالم بحسب الذات، وأنَّ الضَّرورة بحسب الوصف ؛ يُقابلها الإمكان المقيد بحين الوصف، وأنّ الضَّرورةً بحسب الوقتِ المعيَّن; يُقابلها الإمكان بحسب ذلك الوقت، وأن الضرورة بحسب وقت ما ; يقابلها الإمكانُ المقيَّدُ بحسب الزَّمان، وأنَّ الدَّوامَ بحسب الذَّاتِ; يُقابله الإطلاقُ بحسب الذَّاتِ، وأنَّ الدَّوامَ بحسبِ الوصفِ; يُقابلهُ الإطلاق المفيد بحين ذلك الوصف . (قَوْلُهُ : وَأَمَّا النَّقِيْضُ ... إلخ) أي داع إلى تقدير أمَّا في كلام المصنف المحوِجِ لإضمار الفاء معَ المبتدأ ، مع عدم ملائمته للسّياق؟ والأظهرُ والأخصرُ أنْ يقول : والنَّقيضُ لِلمركَّب المفهوم . . . إلخ . (قَوْلُهُ : بَيْنَ) ظَرْفٌ لِلمردَّدِ ; أي : شيءٌ رُدّدَ بين أمرين، وهما نقيضا مُزأَيْ المركَّبة . العطار (قَوْلُهُ: وَأَمَّا النَّقِيْضُ لِلْمُرَكَّبِ) أيُّ داعٍ إلى تقدير (أما) في كلام المصنفِ المحوج لإضمار الفاء مع المبتدأ مع عدم ملائمتِهِ لِلسّياق؟ كَذَا في الحاشية، وأجابَ البعضُ بَأنَّ الشَّارِحَ لم يرد بِمَا قَرَّرَ أَنَّ ذلكَ مُقدَّرٌ في كلام المصنفِ، وإِنَّما هو تصرُّفٌ منهُ دعاه إليهِ عْرضُ الرَّبْطِ بينَ قَولِهِ : هذه نقائص البسائط)، وبين كلام المصنفِ . هـ وأقولُ : لَمَّا كانَ أخْذُ نقيض المركَّباتِ أدقَّ مِنَ البسائط ; فيحتاج إلى مزيدِ عناية; أورد أما المفيدة للتأكيد والاهتمام بالحكم الذي بعدها، واعْلَمْ أَنَّ الحملية قدْ تكون شبيهة بالمنفصلة، والمنفصلة قد تكون شبيهة بالحمليَّةِ، فَإِنَّهُ إِذا حُمِلَ على ضوع واحدٍ أمران متقابلان; فإن قدم الموضوع على حرفِ العنادِ كَقولنا : العدد إما زوج وإمَّا فَردٌ ; فالقضيَّةُ حَمليَّةٌ شَبيهة بالمنفصلة، وإنْ أُخْرَ عَنهَا كَقولِنَا : إِمَّا أَنْ يكونَ العدد زوجاً أو فرداً، فهي منفصلة شبيهة بالحملية، وهناكَ حَمليَّةٌ صرفةٌ ومُنفصلةٌ صرفةٌ، وَهُمَا ظاهرانِ ، ثمَّ الحملية والمنفصلة المتشابهان إذا كانتا كُلِّيَّتَيْنِ; لمْ
Chapter: On Contradiction [How to Contradict Compound Modal Propositions]. And as for the contradictory of the compound, it is the understood concept that is disjunctive between the two contradictories of the two parts. Al-Dasūqī: And it is obtained from this: that necessity in terms of essence is countered by possibility general in terms of essence; and necessity in terms of description is countered by possibility restricted to the time of description; and necessity in terms of a specific time is countered by possibility in terms of that time; and necessity in terms of some time is countered by possibility restricted to time; and eternity in terms of essence is countered by absolute in terms of essence; and eternity in terms of description is countered by absolute that is useful at the time of that description. (His statement: 'and as for the contradictory, etc.') – what caused the estimation of 'ammā' in the author's speech, necessitating the containing of 'fa' with the subject, while it is not suitable to the context? The most apparent and concise would be for him to say: 'and the contradictory of the compound is the understood concept... etc.' (His statement: 'between') – it is a circumstance for 'disjunctive'; i.e., a thing that is disjunctive between two things, and they are the two contradictories of the two parts of the compound. Al-ʿAṭṭār: (His statement: 'and as for the contradictory of the compound') – what caused the estimation of 'ammā' in the author's speech... etc. This is in the gloss. And some answered that the commentator did not intend that it is estimated in the author's speech; rather it is his own adaptation motivated by the need for connection between his statement 'these are the contradictions of the simple' and the author's speech. And I say: since taking the contradictory of compounds is more subtle than the simple, it requires extra attention; so he brought 'ammā' which conveys emphasis and care for the judgment after it. And know that the categorical may resemble the disjunctive, and the disjunctive may resemble the categorical. For if two opposite things are predicated on one subject, and the subject is advanced before the particle of contradiction like our statement: 'The number is either even or odd', then the proposition is categorical resembling the disjunctive. And if it is brought in a different way like our statement: 'Either the number is even or odd', then it is disjunctive resembling the categorical. And there is pure categorical and pure disjunctive, and they are apparent. Then the similar categorical and disjunctive, if they are universal; did not...
Source pages p. 665

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the contradiction of compound modal propositions. The definition is given: the contradictory of a compound (murakkab) proposition is a concept (mafhūm) that is disjunctive (muraddad) between the two contradictories of its two parts. In other words, the contradictory of a compound modal proposition is not itself a simple proposition but a disjunction of two simple contradictories. For example, the contradictory of 'Every A is B necessarily' would be a disjunction between 'Some A is not B possibly' and something else, depending on the parts. Then al-Dasūqī summarises a set of correspondences: necessity by essence is countered by possibility general by essence; necessity by description is countered by possibility restricted to the time of description; etc. This gives a map of how the modalities oppose each other. The text then raises a criticism about the use of the Arabic particle 'ammā' (as for) at the beginning of the definition. The commentator (presumably al-Dasūqī) questions why the author used 'ammā' because it seems to require an implied 'fa' (thus) and a subject that is not present. He suggests it would be clearer to simply say 'And the contradictory of the compound...' without 'ammā'. Al-ʿAṭṭār reports that some responded that the commentator (the author of the original sharh) did not intend that 'ammā' was estimated in the original text; rather, it is his own addition to connect with the previous statement about contradictions of simple propositions. Al-ʿAṭṭār himself adds that since handling compounds is more subtle, the 'ammā' is used for emphasis and care. Then he discusses the distinction between categorical (ḥamliyya) and disjunctive (munfaṣila) propositions, noting that they can resemble each other. He gives an example: 'The number is either even or odd' – this is a categorical proposition because it has a single subject ('the number') and two predicates, but it functions like a disjunction. Conversely, 'Either the number is even or odd' is a full disjunctive. This distinction is important for understanding how to treat compound modals because the compound modal itself may be a disjunctive or categorical in form. The passage ends abruptly in the middle of explaining that when the resembling categorical and disjunctive are universal, they ... (cut off). This indicates that the next part would discuss how to find contradictions for such resembling propositions.

منفصلة
شبيهة

Key Takeaway
Categorical and disjunctive propositions can resemble each other; the position of the subject relative to the disjunctive particle determines the classification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

For each, say whether it is pure categorical, pure disjunctive, categorical resembling disjunctive, or disjunctive resembling categorical, and explain your reasoning.
?

The Contradictory of Compound Propositions
Defines the contradictory of a compound proposition and applies it to particular cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the contradictory of a particular compound proposition and express it as a universal categorical disjunctive proposition.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a compound is not a simple negation but a disjunctive concept that oscillates between two contradictories.

This passage refines the concept of contradiction for compound propositions—a crucial tool for determining truth values in complex logical statements. You will learn how to find the contradictory of a particular conditional and why it takes the form of a universal categorical resembling a disjunctive.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
The contradictory of any compound is a 'disjunctive concept' (al-mafhūm al-muraddad) that hovers between the contradictories of the two parts. This means it asserts one of the two contradictories, but without specifying which.
The definition is given in the matn: 'فهو المفهوم المردد بين نقيضي الجزأين'.
2
Recognize the truth conditions
If the original compound is true, the contradictory is false. If the original is false, the contradictory is true. The falsehood of the original arises from both parts being false or one part being false (determinately or indeterminately); in all such cases the disjunctive contradictory holds.
Shaykh al-Islam clarifies that the contradictory 'lifts' one of the parts without specification.
3
Apply to a particular compound
Consider the proposition 'Some J is B not always'. This means some J is B at some times and not B at other times. The contradictory is that this is not the case: there is no J that is sometimes B and sometimes not B.
The Arabic: 'بعض ج ب لا دائماً' means 'some J is B not always'.
4
Determine the resulting form
From the negation of the particular scenario, it follows that every individual J is either always B or always not B. This is a universal categorical proposition that behaves like a disjunctive (a 'man'at al-jam' wa al-khuluw' type).
The author calls this 'الحملية الشبيهة بالمنفصلة' (the categorical resembling the disjunctive).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي النَّقَاقُضِ (كيفيَّةُ التَّناقض في الموجهات المركبة) وأمَّا النَّقيضُ لِلْمُرَكَّبِ فهو المَفْهُومُ الْمُرَدَّدُ بَيْنَ نَقِيضَيِ الجُزْأَيْنِ. (قَوْلُهُ: الْمَفْهُومُ الْمُرَدَّدُ) قال شيخ الإسلام وهو رفع أحد الجزأين لا على التَّعيين؛ لأنَّهُ إذا صدق الأصل؛ كذب هذا الرَّفعُ بالضرورة، ومتى كذب الأصل؛ صدق هذا؛ لأنَّ كذبَهُ إمَّا بكذب الجزأين معاً، أو بكذب أحدهما على التعيين أو لا على التَّعيين، وعلى التَّقادير يتحقَّقُ هذا الرَّفع. وإذا تمهَّدَ هذا فنقولُ: المركَّبةُ إِنْ كَانَتْ جُزئيَّةٌ كَقولِنَا: بعضُ ج ب لا دائماً، يكون معناه بعضُ ج ب تارةً، وليس ب تارةً أُخرى، فنقيضُهَا أنَّه ليس كذلِكَ؛ أي: ليس بعضُ ج بحيثُ يكون ب تارةً، وليس ب أُخرى فيكونُ كُلُّ واحدٍ واحدٍ إما ب دائماً أو ليس ب دائماً؛ لأنَّهُ لَمَّا لم يكن بعضُ مِنَ الأبعاض بحيث يكون ب تارةٌ وليس ب أُخرى؛ كانَ كُلُّ ج إما ب ولا يكون ليس ب أصلاً، وإما ليس ب ولا يكون ب أصلاً، فنقيضُ الجزئية هو الحمليَّةُ الشَّبيهة بالمنفصلة.
Chapter on contradiction [how contradiction works in composite modal propositions]. As for the contradictory of the compound, it is the concept that is disjunctively distributed between the two contradictories of the two parts. (His saying: 'the disjunctively distributed concept') Shaykh al-Islam said: it is the lifting of one of the two parts without specification; because if the original is true, this lifting is necessarily false, and whenever the original is false, this lifting is true; because its falsehood is either by both parts being false together, or by one of them being false determinately or indeterminately, and in all cases this lifting is realized. And when this is established, we say: the compound, if it is particular, like our saying 'some J is B not always', its meaning is that some J is B sometimes, and not B at other times. So its contradictory is that it is not so; i.e., there is not some J such that it is B sometimes and not B at other times. Then every single individual is either always B or always not B; because since there is no part of the parts that is B sometimes and not B at other times, every J is either B and never not B, or not B and never B. So the contradictory of the particular is the categorical proposition resembling the disjunctive.
Source pages p. 665

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory of a compound proposition and applies it to particular compounds. The author begins by stating the definition: the contradictory of a compound is a disjunctive concept that oscillates between the two contradictories of the two parts. This means that when you have a compound proposition (e.g., a conditional or a disjunctive), its contradictory is not a simple negation of each part separately, but rather a statement that one of the two parts' contradictories holds, without specifying which. The commentary from Shaykh al-Islam clarifies: this is like 'raising' (i.e., negating) one of the two parts indeterminately; if the original is true, the contradictory is necessarily false, and if the original is false, the contradictory is true because the falsehood of the original arises from falsehood of both parts or of one part determinately or indeterminately. Then the author applies this to a particular compound proposition: 'Some J is B not always' means that some J is B at some times and not B at other times. Its contradictory is that this is not the case; i.e., there is no J that is sometimes B and sometimes not B. This forces the conclusion that every J is either always B or always not B—a categorical proposition that resembles a disjunctive (i.e., a universal categorical disjunction, actually a 'man'at al-jam' wa al-khuluw' type). Thus, the contradictory of a particular compound is not itself a particular compound but a universal categorical of a special kind. The author emphasizes that this is the contradictory of the particular compound, not a simple disjunctive, because the simple disjunctive (like 'either some J is always B or some J is always not B') would not be equivalent to the required contradictory when the proposition is particular.

النقيض
المركب
المفهوم المردد
الحملية الشبيهة بالمنفصلة

The contradictory of a particular compound proposition is a universal categorical disjunctive that negates the existence of mixed cases.

Contradictory of a Compound: Exclusive Disjunction Rule
Rule for finding contradictory of compound propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the contradictory of any compound proposition using the rule of exclusive disjunction and justify why inclusive disjunction fails.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a compound is an exclusive disjunction of the contradictories of its parts.

This lesson explores a precise rule from Arabic logic for negating compound propositions (like conjunctions or conditionals). The rule states that the contradictory is not a simple negation of each part, but an exclusive disjunction (māni‘at al-khuluw) of the contradictories. This principle is crucial for accurate reasoning in Islamic sciences, especially when negating legal or theological statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound and its parts
Break the compound proposition into its immediate components. For example, 'Zayd is in the house and Amr is in the market' has two parts: 'Zayd is in the house' and 'Amr is in the market'.
Only binary compounds are considered; for more parts, the rule extends similarly.
2
Form the contradictories of each part
For each part, write its contradictory (negation). For 'Zayd is in the house', the contradictory is 'Zayd is not in the house'.
Ensure the negation is exact: not the opposite but the contradictory.
3
Combine with exclusive disjunction
Join the two contradictories using 'or' (aw) but with the condition that they cannot both be false. This is the exclusive disjunction: exactly one part is true.
The text insists on māni‘at al-khuluw (prevents joint falsehood) to cover all falsity cases of the original.
4
Test truth conditions
Check that the resulting disjunction is true exactly when the original compound is false. For a conjunction, the original is true only when both parts are true, so the contradictory must be false in that case. Exclusive disjunction is false when both parts are true, fulfilling the requirement.
Inclusive disjunction would be true when both parts are true, failing contradiction.
5
Apply to other compounds
The rule applies to any compound that is true only under specific conditions of its parts. Adapt the method for conditionals or other connectives by analyzing their truth conditions.
The passage hints that for some compounds, scholars debated whether the contradictory should be a categorical resembling a disjunction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي التَّنَاقُضِ
بالحقيقة: منفصلةٌ مانعة الخلوّ، مركَّبَةٌ من نقيضي الجزأين، فيكون طريق أخذِ نقيض المركَّبةِ، أن تُحلَّلَ المركَّبةُ إلى الجزأين، ويؤخذ لكلِّ جزء نقيضُه، ويركَّبَ من نقيضي الجزأين منفصلة مانعة الخلو
الدسوقي

وهو : أنَّ المركَّبَةَ تُناقضُها مُنفصلةٌ مانعة خلوّ ; إذ النَّقيضُ على هذا الوجه ليس بشرطية أصلاً، وإِنَّما كانَ النَّقيضُ هو المفهوم المردَّدَ الَّذِي هو مُنفصلة مانعة خلو في الحقيقة؛ لأنَّ المركَّبَ يكذب بكذب أحدِ جُزأَيْهِ .
(قَوْلُهُ : بِالْحَقِيقَةِ) أي: في الحقيقةِ .

مع تصريحِهِم بأنَّهُ في المركَّباتِ مُنفصلة شبيهة بالحمليّة، وأمَّا جَعْلُهُ حمليَّةٌ شبيهةً بالمنفصلة؛ إنَّما أورد على سبيل البحثِ معهُم كَمَا سَننقلُه .
(قَوْلُهُ : مُنْفَصِلَةٌ مَانِعَةُ الْخُلُوِّ إِنَّما اعتبر ذلك ليكونَ مُكذِّباً للمركَّبة على كُلِّ احتمال، فإنَّ المركَّبة لا تكون صادقةٌ إلَّا بصدق جزأيْهَا ، والمفهوم المردَّدُ إنْ كانَ صادق الجزأين أوِ الأَوَّلِ فقط أوِ الثَّاني فقط ; يُكذِّبُ جُزأي: المركبةِ قطعاً بكذب مُجزأيْهَا معاً أو الأوَّلِ فقط أوِ الثَّاني فقط، فإِنَّهُ بخلافِ مَا لَو اعتُبِرَ الانفصالُ الحقيقي، فإنَّهُ لا يُشيرُ حينئذٍ إلى تكذيبها بكذب جزئيْهَا معاً، أو منع الجمع فقط فإِنَّهُ لا يشير إلى تكذيبها بكذبِ جُزأيْهَا معاً، وجَعْلُ النَّقيض مُنفصلة مانعة خُلُوِّ هوَ ما في شرح المصنفِ لِلرِّسالة وغيره، قال بعضُ الأفاضل(۱): وفيه بحث؛ لأنَّ
(۱) (قولُه : بعض الأفاضل) هو مير أبو الفتح في شرح المتن، نقلَهُ عنهُ رجب أفندي في حاشيته على هذا الكتاب ا.هـ. منه .
Chapter on Contradiction. In reality: an exclusive disjunction that prevents joint falsehood (māni‘at al-khuluw), composed of the contradictories of the two parts. So the method of taking the contradictory of a compound is: the compound is analyzed into its two parts, and for each part its contradictory is taken, and from the two contradictories an exclusive disjunction is composed. Al-Dassuqi. And it is: the compound is contradicted by an exclusive disjunction; for the contradictory in this manner is not a conditional at all; rather the contradictory is the disjunctive concept which is an exclusive disjunction in reality; because the compound is false by the falsity of one of its two parts. His statement: 'in reality' means truly. His statement: 'the two parts' means those from which the compound is composed. His statement: 'so it becomes... etc.' is a branching on his statement 'composed of... etc.'. His statement: 'is analyzed' means broken down. His statement: 'exclusive disjunction' means not one that prevents joint truth, because the disjunction can be true with either part. Al-‘Attar: with their statement that in compounds it is a disjunction resembling the categorical; and as for making it a categorical resembling the disjunction, it was only presented as a discussion with them as we will transmit. His statement: 'exclusive disjunction' was considered only to make it falsify the compound in every probability, because the compound is only true by the truth of both its parts, and the disjunctive concept if it is true in both parts or the first only or the second only; it definitely falsifies the two parts of the compound by the falsity of both its parts together or the first only or the second only; unlike if one considers real disjunction, for it does not then indicate its falsity by the falsity of both parts together, or it prevents joint truth only, so it does not indicate its falsity by the falsity of both parts together. And making the contradictory an exclusive disjunction is what is in the commentator's explanation of the treatise and others. Some eminent figures said: there is a discussion in it, because... (1) His statement: 'some eminent figures' is Mir Abu al-Fath in his commentary on the text, transmitted from him by Rajab Afandi in his gloss on this book – end. From me.
Source pages p. 667

Commentary
This passage is a formal section (faṣl) on contradiction (tanāquḍ) of compound propositions. The author states the rule: the contradictory of a compound proposition (i.e., a conjunction or a conditional with multiple parts) is, in reality, an exclusive disjunction (munfaṣila māni‘at al-khuluw) composed of the contradictories of its parts. This means if we have a compound like 'A and B', its contradictory is 'not-A or not-B' but with the condition that they cannot both be false (exclusive disjunction). The rule is explained: to find the contradictory, decompose the compound into its parts, take the contradictory of each part, and then combine them with an exclusive disjunction. The author then glosses the meaning: the contradictory is not a conditional proposition (sharṭiyya) but rather the 'disjunctive concept' (al-mafhūm al-muraddad) which is effectively an exclusive disjunction. The reason is that the compound is false if at least one part is false (for conjunction) or if the antecedent is true and consequent false (for conditional), but the exclusive disjunction covers all those cases. The commentary by Dassuqi and others clarifies that the disjunction must be exclusive (preventing joint falsehood) to ensure that every truth value of the disjunction corresponds to a falsity of the compound. For example, if the compound is true only when both parts are true, then the contradictory must be false when both parts are true. An exclusive disjunction (true only when exactly one part is true) is false when both are true, and true otherwise. If it were a non-exclusive disjunction (inclusive or), it would also be true when both parts are true, which would not correctly contradict the compound (which is true in that case). The author then notes a debate: some scholars argue that in compounds, the contradictory is a disjunction resembling a categorical (ḥamliyya shabīha bi al-munfaṣila), not this rule. The passage ends with a reference to a discussion by Mir Abu al-Fath and Rajab Afandi about a problem in this rule.

نقيض
المفهوم المردد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must the contradictory of a compound be an exclusive disjunction (māni‘at al-khuluw) rather than an inclusive disjunction?
A) Because the compound is true when both parts are true, and the exclusive disjunction is false in that case.
B) Because the compound is false when both parts are false, and the exclusive disjunction is true in that case.
C) Because the inclusive disjunction is too weak to contradict the compound.
D) Because the scholars agreed on exclusive disjunction for all compounds.

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of any compound proposition must be an exclusive disjunction of the contradictories of its parts to correctly oppose the truth conditions of the original.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct the contradictory of the compound statement: 'Salah is valid if one faces the qibla and one is in a state of purity.' (Hint: The compound is a conjunction of conditions.) Use the exclusive disjunction rule.
?
Explain why an inclusive disjunction (or both) would fail to be the contradictory of the compound 'Fasting is obligatory in Ramadan and zakat is obligatory on wealth above nisab' according to the rule in the passage.
